Dispute on Kafalah for the Deceased: Usul Analysis
Presents a usul dispute on kafalah after death with Hanafi response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of dhimma cessation to evaluate a hadith-based dispute on kafalah for the deceased.

Core Idea
Death dissolves the dhimma — kafalah after death is invalid in Hanafi usul.

This passage presents an internal Hanafi dispute on whether a valid kafalah (suretyship) can be made on behalf of a deceased person. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it is invalid because the dhimma (legal personality) ends at death. His two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, alongside the three other Imams, argue it is valid, citing the hadith of Jabir. The passage shows how the Hanafi school defends its position by critically analyzing the opposing hadith evidence and applying the usul principle that the dhimma is extinguished upon death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
First, note Abu Hanifa's position: 'لا كفالة بعده' (no kafalah after death). Then, note the Sahibayn's position: 'تصح الكفالة عن الميت' (kafalah for the deceased is valid).
This is a clear intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
2
Extract the opposing proof
Identify the hadith of Jabir cited by the Sahibayn. Abu Qatadah said: 'هما الديناران علي يا رسول الله' and the Prophet prayed over the deceased. The Sahibayn argue that this shows a valid kafalah after death, and that death does not cancel the debt.
Also note the additional argument: debt remains after death in the afterlife.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response offers alternative interpretations: the hadith may refer to a promise of payment (وعد الأداء) or an acknowledgment of a prior kafalah (إقرار بكفالة سابقة). The afterlife accountability is about sin, not dhimma continuity.
The commentator notes support for the second interpretation from Sahih Ibn Hibban.
4
Connect to usul principle
The core Hanafi principle is that death dissolves the dhimma. Without a dhimma, no new obligation (including kafalah) can be created. The estate is responsible, not a new guarantee.
The dhimma is a key concept: it is the capacity to incur obligations.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, if someone dies with unpaid debts, a new kafalah contract cannot be formed according to Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn allow it. The mufti follows Abu Hanifa's view as the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.
This affects how creditors seek payment: they must go to the estate, not a guarantor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ضم الذمة ولا كفالة بعده. وعندهما (أبي يوسف ومحمد) تصح الكفالة عن الميت، وبه قالت الأئمة الثلاثة، لحديث جابر إن أبا قتادة قال: هما الديناران علي يا رسول الله، فصلى عليه فكفل أبو قتادة عن الميت، ولأن الموت لا يبرئ الميت عن الدين، ولذا (لعدم برائته) يطالب بالدين في الآخرة إجماعاً، ويصح التبرع للميت بالأداء عنه، أي بأداء الغير دينه عنه. والجواب عنه أنه يحتمل عدة الأداء، لا الكفالة، ويحتمل أن يكون إقراراً بكفالة سابقة، وفيه ما فيه من تأيد الجواب الثاني قال في تعليقه: فيه إشارة إلى ما في صحيح ابن حبان فقال أبو قتادة: أنا أكفل به أي بالوفاء على الكفالة السابقة، والمطالبة الأخروية باعتبار الإثم، أي إثم عدم إيصال الدين إلى صاحبه، لا تفتقر إلى بقاء ذمة الميت، وصحة التبرع لبقاء الدين من جهة من له الدين، فإن سقوط الأداء بالموت بضرورة فوت المحل (محل فعل الأداء) فيظهر هذا السقوط في حق من عليه الدين، دون حق من له الدين، فيبقى الدين من جهة من له.
[Abu Hanifa said:] The guarantee is on the estate, and no kafalah after [death]. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), kafalah for the deceased is valid, and the three Imams said this, based on the hadith of Jabir that Abu Qatadah said: 'These two dinars are upon me, O Messenger of Allah,' so he (the Prophet) prayed over him, and Abu Qatadah stood as kafil for the deceased. And because death does not absolve the deceased from the debt, and therefore (due to his non-absolution) he is demanded (for the debt) in the Hereafter by consensus, and donation on behalf of the deceased by paying off his debt is valid, i.e., a third party paying his debt for him. The response to this is that [the hadith] could be interpreted as a promise of payment, not kafalah, and it could be an acknowledgment of a prior kafalah. And there is in it what supports the second response. He said in his commentary: It contains a reference to what is in Sahih Ibn Hibban: Abu Qatadah said: 'I will stand as kafil for it,' i.e., for payment, based on the prior kafalah. And the demand in the afterlife is based on sin, i.e., the sin of not delivering the debt to its owner; it does not require the continued existence of the deceased's dhimma. And the validity of donation is due to the persistence of the debt from the perspective of the creditor. For the obligation to pay drops upon death due to the necessary loss of the locus (the locus of the act of payment), so this drop appears from the perspective of the debtor, not from the perspective of the creditor; thus the debt remains from the creditor's side.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage presents a usul dispute regarding the validity of kafalah (suretyship) on behalf of a deceased person. The Hanafi school is split: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that no valid kafalah can be made after death because the obligation is on the estate (dhimma is dissolved), while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, along with the three other Imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad), hold that kafalah for the deceased is valid. Their main proof is the hadith of Jabir: Abu Qatadah volunteered to pay two dinars owed by a deceased man, and the Prophet prayed over the deceased after that. They also argue that death does not cancel the debt; the deceased is still held accountable in the afterlife, and voluntary payment on his behalf is valid. The commentator then presents the Hanafi response: the hadith is ambiguous—it may refer to a promise to pay or an acknowledgment of a prior suretyship, not a new kafalah after death. Moreover, the afterlife accountability is about sin, not about the continued existence of the dhimma. Thus, Abu Hanifa's position is upheld through careful textual analysis. This discussion illustrates the Hanafi usul principle that the dhimma (legal personality) ceases upon death, affecting obligations like kafalah.

Key Terms
كفالة (kafalah): A contract of suretyship where one person (kafil) guarantees the debt or obligation of another.
ذمة (dhimma): The legal personality and capacity to incur obligations; considered to be extinguished upon death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary basis for Abu Hanifa's ruling that kafalah for the deceased is invalid?
A) The hadith of Jabir is not authentic.
B) Death dissolves the dhimma, and the hadith can be interpreted differently.
C) The Sahibayn agree with Abu Hanifa.
D) Kafalah is only valid for the living.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the dhimma ends at death, so a new kafalah after death is invalid; the hadith evidence is reinterpreted to align with this principle.
